# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

64-assistanttext-
I've successfully found and documented all the Go source files related to Grafana's configuration loading system. Here's a summary of what I discovered:

## Key Files Found:

**Core Configuration System:**
- `pkg/setting/setting.go` - Main configuration loader with INI parser, environment variable override logic, and sensitive value masking
- `pkg/setting/expanders.go` - Variable expansion for environment variables and file references
- `pkg/setting/provider.go` - Settings provider interface and OSS implementation that handles redaction
- `conf/defaults.ini` - Default configuration values for all sections

**API Endpoint:**
- `pkg/api/admin.go` - Implementation of `/api/admin/settings` endpoint with authorization and redaction

**Configuration Sections (23+ files):**
- Multiple `setting_*.go` files that handle specific configuration sections (auth, database, server, SMTP, etc.)

## Configuration Loading Chain:

1. **Load defaults.ini** - Base configuration with all default values
2. **Command-line default properties** (cfg:default.*)
3. **Custom INI file** (conf/custom.ini)
4. **Environment variable overrides** (GF_SECTION_KEY format via `applyEnvVariableOverrides()`)
5. **Command-line overrides** (cfg:*)
6. **Variable expansion** - `$VAR`, `${VAR}`, `$__file{path}` syntax via `expandConfig()`

## Sensitive Value Masking:

The `RedactedValue()` function in `pkg/setting/setting.go` (lines 660-709) masks sensitive configuration by matching patterns for PASSWORD, SECRET, TOKEN, ENCRYPTION_KEY, CERTIFICATE, etc., replacing them with `*********`.

The API endpoint applies this masking through the settings provider's `Current()` method, ensuring the `/api/admin/settings` endpoint never exposes sensitive values.

Complete details have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

First loads defaults from `conf/defaults.ini` using the gopkg.in/ini.v1 library\\n   - Then applies configuration overrides in the following priority order:\\n     - Command-line default properties (default.*)\\n     - Custom INI file (conf/custom.ini)\\n     - Environment variable overrides\\n     - Command-line overrides (cfg:*)\\n     - Variable expansion (environment variables and file references)\\n\\n2. **Default Values (conf/defaults.ini)**\\n   - Grafana stores all default configuration values in `conf/defaults.ini`\\n   - This file is loaded first and serves as the base configuration\\n   - Custom configuration only needs to specify values that differ from defaults\\n\\n3. **Environment Variable Override Logic (pkg/setting/setting.go:744-759)**\\n   - `applyEnvVariableOverrides()` checks for environment variables using the `EnvKey()` function\\n   - The `EnvKey()` function (line 855-861) converts section and key names to the format `GF_SECTION_KEY`\\n   - For example, `database.name` becomes `GF_DATABASE_NAME`\\n   - Environment variables override values from the INI file\\n\\n4. **Variable Expansion (pkg/setting/expanders.go)**\\n   - `expandConfig()` function processes configuration values containing variable references\\n   - Supports two types of expanders:\\n     - `envExpander`: Expands `$VARIABLE_NAME` or `${VARIABLE_NAME}` syntax to environment variable values\\n     - `fileExpander`: Expands `$__file{/path/to/file}` syntax to read values from files\\n   - Environment variable expansion for HOSTNAME has special handling for empty values\\n\\n5. **Command-Line Overrides (pkg/setting/setting.go:863-913)**\\n   - `applyCommandLineDefaultProperties()` handles `cfg:default.*` arguments\\n   - `applyCommandLineProperties()` handles `cfg:*` arguments\\n   - Command-line arguments have the highest priority in the override chain\\n\\n## Configuration Sections with Defaults\\n\\nMultiple specialized configuration files handle different sections:\\n- `setting_anonymous.go`: [auth.anonymous] section\\n- `setting_auth_proxy.go`: [auth_proxy] section\\n- `setting_azure.go`: [azure] and [auth.azuread] sections\\n- `setting_smtp.go`: [smtp] section\\n- `setting_jwt.go`: [auth.jwt] section\\n- `setting_unified_alerting.go`: [unified_alerting] section\\n- `setting_grpc.go`: [grpc_server] section\\n- `setting_remote_cache.go`: [remote_cache] section\\n- `setting_secrets_manager.go`: [secrets.management] section\\nAnd many others, each reading default values using the `MustString()`, `MustBool()`, `MustDuration()` methods with sensible defaults\\n\\n## Sensitive Configuration Value Masking\\n\\n1. **RedactedValue Function (pkg/setting/setting.go:660-709)**\\n   - Masks sensitive configuration values to prevent accidental exposure\\n   - Applies regex patterns to identify sensitive keys containing:\\n     - PASSWORD, SECRET, PRIVATE_KEY, CERTIFICATE, ENCRYPTION_KEY, TOKEN, API_TOKEN, etc.\\n   - Returns `*********` (RedactedPassword constant) for matching sensitive keys\\n   - Includes exceptions for analytics providers (RUDDERSTACK, APPLICATION_INSIGHTS, SENTRY)\\n   - Falls back to URL redaction for values that appear to be URLs with credentials\\n\\n2. **API Settings Endpoint (pkg/api/admin.go:29-35)**\\n   - `AdminGetSettings()` endpoint retrieves current settings from the configuration\\n   - Calls `getAuthorizedSettings()` to filter settings based on user permissions\\n   - Returns settings through the settings provider which applies `RedactedValue()` to mask sensitive data\\n   - The provider's `Current()` method (pkg/setting/provider.go:118-129) creates a settings copy with redacted values\\n\\n3. **Settings Provider (pkg/setting/provider.go)**\\n   - `OSSImpl.Current()` returns a `SettingsBag` (map[string]map[string]string) of all current settings\\n   - Each value is passed through `RedactedValue()` with the full environment key name\\n   - `OSSImpl.CurrentVerbose()` returns settings with source information (DB vs System)\\n   - The provider enforces fine-grained access control via RBAC scopes: `settings:*`, `settings:SECTION:*`, `settings:SECTION:KEY`\\n\\n## Configuration Flow Summary\\n\\nThe configuration loading flow in `pkg/setting/setting.go:Load()` \u2192 `loadConfiguration()` is:\\n1. Load defaults.ini\\n2. Apply command-line default properties (cfg:default.*)\\n3. Load and merge custom.ini\\n4. Apply environment variable overrides (GF_* format)\\n5. Parse sections via specialized setting_*.go files\\n\\nWhen the `/api/admin/settings` endpoint is called, the current configuration is retrieved via `pkg/setting/provider.go:OSSImpl.Current()` which applies redaction before returning to the client, ensuring sensitive values like passwords, API tokens, and encryption keys are never exposed in the API response.\"\n}\n",
